				<div id="content">
					<div class="marginator">
					
										
					<a href="#sidebar-left" id="skip-to-nav">Skip to Navigation</a>

									
						<h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Slavic Studies</h1>
					<div class="columns main-columns">


						

						<div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">

							
																												
							<div class="clear-block">
								

<article id="node-1144" class="main-article node">







  <div class="content">
        
    <p>The <a href="https://www.brown.edu/academics/slavic-studies/graduate">Department of Slavic Languages</a> offers a comprehensive doctoral program in Slavic studies specializing  in Russian literature and culture, in modern Czech culture, and in  Polish literature and culture.</p>
<p>The program has a strong interdisciplinary focus and students are  expected to work with departmental faculty as well as with faculty in  related fields, such as comparative literature, theater, history, art  history, modern culture and media, and political science. The program  will train flexible and innovative scholars able to address varying  teaching and research needs in the future job market. We particularly  target advanced students who would come to Brown with a strong  background in at least one of the program's key disciplines (literature,  language, culture, theater, social sciences). Students receive close  guidance and are mentored in the pedagogy of language and  literature/culture teaching.</p>
<p><strong>Additional resources:</strong> Slavic library and reading room, commons room for lectures and presentations, audio-visual equipment.</p>
<p><strong>Completion Requirements</strong><br /><strong>A.M.: </strong>Eight courses, approved by the department</p>
<p><strong>Ph.D.: </strong>Sixteen courses, including five graduate seminars, and two to  four courses in a secondary field of study; theory and methods of  foreign language teaching, reading knowledge of the second language  related to the student's specialization; teaching; qualifying  examinations; dissertation and defense.</p>
<p><strong>Admission Information</strong><br /><strong>Admission Requirements:</strong> Advanced  competence in Russian. Writing sample in English (12-15 pages).  Knowledge/interest in another Slavic language (preferably Czech or  Polish) in encouraged but not required.</p>
<p><strong>GRE General: </strong>Required<br /><strong>GRE Subject: </strong>Not required<br /><strong>Application Deadline:</strong> January 7</p>
  </div>

	
  <div class="clear-block">
    <div class="meta">

<a href="/academics/slavic-studies/"><img src="/academics/slavic-studies/sites/brown.edu.academics.slavic-studies/files/pawtucket_simple_banner_image.jpg" /></a>
<div class="banner-text">
				<h1><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/" title="" accesskey="2"><span class="site-title"></span></a></h1><div id="site-slogan" class="slogan banner-subtext"></div>			</div></section>
		    
  <!-- Layout -->
  <div id="content">
    <div class="marginator">
                  <div class="columns main-columns">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Courses for Fall 2017</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                              <div id="tabs-wrapper" class="clear-block">
            <ul class="tabs primary">
              <li ><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/czch">CZCH</a></li>
<li ><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/plsh">PLSH</a></li>
<li ><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/russ">RUSS</a></li>
<li ><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/slav">SLAV</a></li>

            </ul>
          </div>
                                        <div class="clear-block"> <div class="content">



		<div class="course-section" id="CZCH">
				<h3>CZCH</h3>
			
				<ul class="course-list">
										<li id="CZCH0100">
					<h4>Introductory Czech</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">Introduces the performance of basic tasks in Standard Czech, highlights of Czech culture, and a worldview of a nation uniquely located on the threshold of western and eastern Europe. Emphasis on oral communication. Five meetings per week and use of audio/visual materials. Enrollment limited to 18. </div>
		
					<div class="sections">

WRIT </div>

										<li id="RUSS1340">
					<h4>The Russian Novel</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">When one considers the impact of Russian literature on world literature, one thinks first of all of the novel. And indeed, since the late nineteenth century its readers all over the world could not resist its artistic powers. The course explores selected Russian novels form the nineteenth- to the twenty-first century. Our in-depth (slow) reading and discussions will be guided by the questions concerning the stylistic peculiarities of the novel, and its development in changing historical and cultural contexts. The course includes: Gogol’s Dead Souls, Goncharov’s Oblomov, Dostoevsky’s Idiot, Bely’s Petersburg, Nabokov’s Mary, Platonov’s Chevengur, among others. WRIT </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=15159">RUSS 1340 S01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Oklot</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																					
																								</div>
						
				</li>
										<li id="RUSS1440">
					<h4>Imagining Moscow: Utopia and Urban Spaces in 20th-Century Russian Culture</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">The course explores the role of Moscow in the Russian collective imagery throughout the 20th century. We will study how different utopian visions of the city in art, literature, film, and architecture affected the radical transformations of its urban landscape from the October Revolution to the present. We will start with the 1920s and 1930s, when the image of a new Moscow became closely associated with the creation of new socialist ways of life, and conclude with the neoliberal and neoimperialist facelift of the city in the post-Soviet period, retracing a history of 20th-century Russian culture through its urban imagination. WRIT </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">

						</div>

				</li>
										<li id="RUSS1860">
					<h4>Chekhov</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">Commemorating the hundredth anniversary of the death of the great Russian playwright and short-story writer, this course will examine Chekhov's innovations in the genre of the short story and in modern theater, as well as his ongoing influences in world literature. Themes include the nature of the Chekhovian comic, subversion of the dominant literary and cultural paradigms and myths, representations of gender and sexuality. In English. One of the tasks is to improve students' writing skills. WRIT </div>

				</li>
										<li id="RUSS1885">
					<h4>Literature and Art of the Russian Avant-Garde</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">Examines the Russian avant-garde between 1912, the year of the first Russian futurist manifesto, and early 1930s when Social Realism became this only sanctioned style of art. This, arguably the most vibrant period in Russian art, permeated with unprecedented sense of creative and political urgency, coincided with the WWI and the Russian Revolution, which provide historical contexts for the analyzed works. Also stresses aesthetic and historic interconnections between the Russian and western avant-gardes. Includes the works of poetry, prose, literary manifestos, book design, painting, and film by such artists as Pasternak, Mayakovsky, Khlebnikov, Mandelshtam, Meyerhold, Malevich, Rodchenko, Eisenstein, among others.  WRIT </div>

	<div class="course-section" id="SLAV">
				<h3>SLAV</h3>
			
				<ul class="course-list">
										<li id="SLAV1300">
					<h4>Sociolinguistics (with Case Studies on the Former USSR and Eastern Europe)</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">This seminar course examines the relationship between language and society: e.g. gender and language, politeness, terms of address, conversational analysis, dialects and language, language variation and social class, language policies and their consequences, language and national/ethnic identity. Case-study readings cover (but are not limited to) linguistic situations in East Europe, Russia, and the former republics of the USSR. Knowledge of Slavic languages not required. Open to advanced undergraduate and graduate students. Freshmen and sophomores who demonstrate their knowledge of the basic notions in linguistics or their familiarity with the former USSR and East Europe may enroll with the instructor’s written permission. Enrollment limited to 20.  DPLL WRIT </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=15148">SLAV 1300 S01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Fidler</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																					
																								</div>
						
				</li>
										<li id="SLAV1950">
					<h4>Independent Study</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">Independent research project on topics in Slavic Studies. Enrollment permitted only after the written proposal (instructions in the department office) is submitted to the Concentration Advisor and Chair of the department (deadline: the last day of <i>Add a course without fee</i> period during the semester when the project is undertaken). Please check Banner for the correct section number and CRN to use when registering for this course. Each section limited to 10 students; instructor permission required. </div>

										<li id="SLAV1981">
					<h4>Independent Research in the Slavic Language(s)</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">Independent research on various topics in Slavic cultures. Reading, discussion, research must be done in the chosen Slavic language (Czech/Russian).  Close work with faculty on project is expected. Prerequisites: minimum RUSS0600/CZCH 0610 (3rd year-level) or placement evaluation by Russian or Czech language coordinator. Enrollment permitted only after the written proposal (instructions in the department office) is submitted to the Concentration Advisor and Chair of the department (deadline: the last day of <i>Add a course without fee</i> period during the semester when the project is undertaken).  Each section limited to 10 students; instructor permission required. </div>

<script type="text/javascript">
	// @todo: make show/hide link dynamically generated
	$(document).ready(function(){
	
		$(".course-list .additional-sections").hide();

		// add additional sections toggle link
		$(".course-list .additional-sections").each(function(i,el){
			var numSections = $(".section", $(this)).length;
			numSections = (numSections == 1) ? numSections + " additional section" : numSections + " additional sections";
			var anchor = $(this).parents("li").attr('id');
			$(this).after('<span class="section-count">[<a href="#' + anchor + '">Show ' + numSections + '</a>]</span>');
		});

		// now add the show/hide event listeners		
		$(".section-count").each(function(i,el){
			$("a", this).bind("click keypress", function(){
				$(".additional-sections", $(this).parents("li")).slideToggle("fast");
				window.location.hash = $(this).attr("href");
				if($(this).html().match(/Show/)) {
					$(this).html($(this).html().replace("Show", "Hide"));
				} else if($(this).html().match(/Hide/)) {
					$(this).html($(this).html().replace("Hide", "Show"));
				}
				this.text(($('#toggle').text() == 'Show more') ? 'Show less' : 'Show more');
				return false;
			});
		});
		
		if (window.location.hash) {
			var hash = window.location.hash;
			if(hash.match(/#[0-9]{4}/)) {
				$(hash +  " .additional-sections").slideDown("fast");
				$(hash +  " a[href='"+hash+"']").html($(hash +  " a[href='"+hash+"']").html().replace("Show", "Hide"));
			}
		}

	});
</script>

				<section id="banner" class="marginator sub-banner">
<a href="/academics/slavic-studies/"><img src="/academics/slavic-studies/sites/brown.edu.academics.slavic-studies/files/pawtucket_simple_banner_image.jpg" /></a>
<div class="banner-text">
				<h1><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/" title="" accesskey="2"><span class="site-title"></span></a></h1><div id="site-slogan" class="slogan banner-subtext"></div>			</div></section>
		    
  <!-- Layout -->
  <div id="content">
    <div class="marginator">
                  <div class="columns main-columns">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Courses for Fall 2017</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                              <div id="tabs-wrapper" class="clear-block">
            <ul class="tabs primary">
              <li class="active" ><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/czch" class="active">CZCH</a></li>
<li ><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/plsh">PLSH</a></li>
<li ><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/russ">RUSS</a></li>
<li ><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/slav">SLAV</a></li>

            </ul>
          </div>
                                        <div class="clear-block"> <div class="content">



		<div class="course-section" id="czch">
			
				<ul class="course-list">
										<li id="CZCH0100">
					<h4>Introductory Czech</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">Introduces the performance of basic tasks in Standard Czech, highlights of Czech culture, and a worldview of a nation uniquely located on the threshold of western and eastern Europe. Emphasis on oral communication. Five meetings per week and use of audio/visual materials. Enrollment limited to 18. </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=15149">CZCH 0100 S01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Fidler</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																					
																								</div>
						
				</li>
										<li id="CZCH0410D">
					<h4>Czechs and the Big Brother: Czech Lands in the 1980s</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">Events in Czechoslovakia in the late 1980's as represented in the Oscar-winning film <i>Kolja</i>. The Velvet Revolution and the Czech perspective on Russia. Readings from different genres. Equal emphasis on language acquisition, including Colloquial Czech. Separate language tasks for two proficiency levels (2nd-3rd year). Conducted in Czech. For students who have completed CZCH 0200 or the equivalent. Enrollment limited to 18. </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=15150">CZCH 0410D S01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Fidler</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																					
																								</div>
						
				</li>
					</ul>
		
	</div> <!-- end .course-section -->



</div>



<script type="text/javascript">
	// @todo: make show/hide link dynamically generated
	$(document).ready(function(){
	
		$(".course-list .additional-sections").hide();

		// add additional sections toggle link
		$(".course-list .additional-sections").each(function(i,el){
			var numSections = $(".section", $(this)).length;
			numSections = (numSections == 1) ? numSections + " additional section" : numSections + " additional sections";
			var anchor = $(this).parents("li").attr('id');
			$(this).after('<span class="section-count">[<a href="#' + anchor + '">Show ' + numSections + '</a>]</span>');
		});

		// now add the show/hide event listeners		
		$(".section-count").each(function(i,el){
			$("a", this).bind("click keypress", function(){
				$(".additional-sections", $(this).parents("li")).slideToggle("fast");
				window.location.hash = $(this).attr("href");
				if($(this).html().match(/Show/)) {
					$(this).html($(this).html().replace("Show", "Hide"));
				} else if($(this).html().match(/Hide/)) {
					$(this).html($(this).html().replace("Hide", "Show"));
				}
				this.text(($('#toggle').text() == 'Show more') ? 'Show less' : 'Show more');
				return false;
			});
		});
		
		if (window.location.hash) {
			var hash = window.location.hash;
			if(hash.match(/#[0-9]{4}/)) {
				$(hash +  " .additional-sections").slideDown("fast");
				$(hash +  " a[href='"+hash+"']").html($(hash +  " a[href='"+hash+"']").html().replace("Show", "Hide"));
			}
		}

	});
</script>

        <div class="item-list">		
                             	<h3 class="current-site"><a href="">Department of Slavic Studies</a></h3>
            
      
        <div class="list">

<script type="text/javascript">
	// @todo: make show/hide link dynamically generated
	$(document).ready(function(){
	
		$(".course-list .additional-sections").hide();

		// add additional sections toggle link
		$(".course-list .additional-sections").each(function(i,el){
			var numSections = $(".section", $(this)).length;
			numSections = (numSections == 1) ? numSections + " additional section" : numSections + " additional sections";
			var anchor = $(this).parents("li").attr('id');
			$(this).after('<span class="section-count">[<a href="#' + anchor + '">Show ' + numSections + '</a>]</span>');
		});

		// now add the show/hide event listeners		
		$(".section-count").each(function(i,el){
			$("a", this).bind("click keypress", function(){
				$(".additional-sections", $(this).parents("li")).slideToggle("fast");
				window.location.hash = $(this).attr("href");
				if($(this).html().match(/Show/)) {
					$(this).html($(this).html().replace("Show", "Hide"));
				} else if($(this).html().match(/Hide/)) {
					$(this).html($(this).html().replace("Hide", "Show"));
				}
				this.text(($('#toggle').text() == 'Show more') ? 'Show less' : 'Show more');
				return false;
			});
		});
		
		if (window.location.hash) {
			var hash = window.location.hash;
			if(hash.match(/#[0-9]{4}/)) {
				$(hash +  " .additional-sections").slideDown("fast");
				$(hash +  " a[href='"+hash+"']").html($(hash +  " a[href='"+hash+"']").html().replace("Show", "Hide"));
			}
		}

	});
</script>

<div class="banner-text">
				<h1><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/" title="" accesskey="2"><span class="site-title"></span></a></h1><div id="site-slogan" class="slogan banner-subtext"></div>			</div></section>
		    
  <!-- Layout -->
  <div id="content">
    <div class="marginator">
                  <div class="columns main-columns">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Courses for Fall 2017</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                              <div id="tabs-wrapper" class="clear-block">
            <ul class="tabs primary">
              <li ><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/czch">CZCH</a></li>
<li ><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/plsh">PLSH</a></li>
<li class="active" ><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/russ" class="active">RUSS</a></li>
<li ><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/slav">SLAV</a></li>

            </ul>
          </div>
                                        <div class="clear-block"> <div class="content">



		<div class="course-section" id="russ">
			
				<ul class="course-list">
										<li id="RUSS0100">
					<h4>Introductory Russian</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">Introduction to Russian language and culture. Oral and written communication in Russian; emphasis on the literary and everyday culture of Russia and the former U.S.S.R., including the changes that have reshaped everyday life for citizens of Russia. Five meetings per week, plus use of audio, video, and web materials.  Enrollment limited to 18. </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=15369">RUSS 0100 S01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>deBenedette</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																				<div class="additional-sections">
															
																		
												<div class="section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=15370">RUSS 0100 S02</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>deBenedette</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
														
																		
												<div class="section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=15371">RUSS 0100 S03</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>deBenedette</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
														
																										</div>
												</div>
						
				</li>
										<li id="RUSS0300">
					<h4>Intermediate Russian</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">Continues development of language proficiency while broadening understanding of contemporary Russian culture via readings in literature and history. Expansion of vocabulary for dealing with conversational topics and review of Russian grammar. Features literary and nonliterary readings in Russian, as well as video and computer resources. Five class meetings per week. Prerequisite: RUSS 0110 or RUSS 0200 or RUSS 0250 or placement by exam.  Enrollment limited to 18. </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=15373">RUSS 0300 S02</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Fenghi</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																				<div class="additional-sections">
															
																		
												<div class="section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=15378">RUSS 0300 C01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Fenghi</dd>
																								<dt>Schedule Code</dt><dd>C: Conference</dd>
															</dl>
						</div>
						
														
																										</div>
												</div>
						
				</li>
										<li id="RUSS0320E">
					<h4>Crime and Punishment through Literature</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">The seminar will explore how texts of different epochs and cultures, ranging from Ancient to Modern and from drama to poem, novel, and film treat the issues of transgression, punishment, justice, and forgiveness. We will examine each text both in terms of its artistic merit and its place within its cultural and historical milieu. Enrollment limited to 20 first-year students. FYS WRIT </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=15160">RUSS 0320E S01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Golstein</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																					
																								</div>
						
				</li>
										<li id="RUSS0500">
					<h4>Advanced Russian</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">Examines selected topics in Russian culture and history as depicted in readings, the media, and Russian and Soviet films. Language work emphasizes increasing facility with spoken Russian and developing writing skills. Includes work on advanced grammar and syntax. Five class meetings per week. Prerequisites: RUSS 0350 or RUSS 0400 or placement. Enrollment limited to 18. </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=15374">RUSS 0500 S01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>deBenedette</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																					
																								</div>
						
				</li>
										<li id="RUSS1110">
					<h4>Special Topics in Russian Studies I: Advanced Reading and Conversation</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">An advanced course recommended for students who are either planning to go or are returning from abroad.  Focus on Russian culture as seen through the prism of Russian poetry.  Extensive classroom discussion and frequent writing assignments. Prerequisite: RUSS 0600 or written permission. May be repeated once with permission from the instructor. Enrollment limited to 18. </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=15163">RUSS 1110 S01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Simankov</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																					
																								</div>
						
				</li>
										<li id="RUSS1290">
					<h4>Russian Literature in Translation I: Pushkin to Dostoevsky</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">Survey of major works of Russian literature of the early and mid-19th century. Authors to be studied include Karamzin, Pushkin, Lermontov, Gogol, Turgenev, Leskov, and Dostoevsky. Lectures and discussion. No knowledge of Russian required. Discussion sections to be arranged.  WRIT </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=15145">RUSS 1290 S01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Levitsky</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																					
																								</div>
						
				</li>
										<li id="RUSS1340">
					<h4>The Russian Novel</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">When one considers the impact of Russian literature on world literature, one thinks first of all of the novel. And indeed, since the late nineteenth century its readers all over the world could not resist its artistic powers. The course explores selected Russian novels form the nineteenth- to the twenty-first century. Our in-depth (slow) reading and discussions will be guided by the questions concerning the stylistic peculiarities of the novel, and its development in changing historical and cultural contexts. The course includes: Gogol’s Dead Souls, Goncharov’s Oblomov, Dostoevsky’s Idiot, Bely’s Petersburg, Nabokov’s Mary, Platonov’s Chevengur, among others. WRIT </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=15159">RUSS 1340 S01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Oklot</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																					
																								</div>
						
				</li>
										<li id="RUSS1440">
					<h4>Imagining Moscow: Utopia and Urban Spaces in 20th-Century Russian Culture</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">The course explores the role of Moscow in the Russian collective imagery throughout the 20th century. We will study how different utopian visions of the city in art, literature, film, and architecture affected the radical transformations of its urban landscape from the October Revolution to the present. We will start with the 1920s and 1930s, when the image of a new Moscow became closely associated with the creation of new socialist ways of life, and conclude with the neoliberal and neoimperialist facelift of the city in the post-Soviet period, retracing a history of 20th-century Russian culture through its urban imagination. WRIT </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=16335">RUSS 1440 S01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Fenghi</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																					
																								</div>
						
				</li>
										<li id="RUSS1860">
					<h4>Chekhov</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">Commemorating the hundredth anniversary of the death of the great Russian playwright and short-story writer, this course will examine Chekhov's innovations in the genre of the short story and in modern theater, as well as his ongoing influences in world literature. Themes include the nature of the Chekhovian comic, subversion of the dominant literary and cultural paradigms and myths, representations of gender and sexuality. In English. One of the tasks is to improve students' writing skills. WRIT </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=15137">RUSS 1860 S01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Evdokimova</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																					
																								</div>
						
				</li>
										<li id="RUSS1885">
					<h4>Literature and Art of the Russian Avant-Garde</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">Examines the Russian avant-garde between 1912, the year of the first Russian futurist manifesto, and early 1930s when Social Realism became this only sanctioned style of art. This, arguably the most vibrant period in Russian art, permeated with unprecedented sense of creative and political urgency, coincided with the WWI and the Russian Revolution, which provide historical contexts for the analyzed works. Also stresses aesthetic and historic interconnections between the Russian and western avant-gardes. Includes the works of poetry, prose, literary manifestos, book design, painting, and film by such artists as Pasternak, Mayakovsky, Khlebnikov, Mandelshtam, Meyerhold, Malevich, Rodchenko, Eisenstein, among others.  WRIT </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=17099">RUSS 1885 S01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Oklot</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																					
																								</div>
						
				</li>
										<li id="RUSS1960">
					<h4>Independent Study</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">Independent research project on topics related to Russian culture. Enrollment permitted only after the written proposal (instructions in the department office) is submitted to the Concentration Advisor and Chair of the department (deadline: the last day of <i>Add a course without fee</i> period during the semester when the project is undertaken).  Please check Banner for the correct section number and CRN to use when registering for this course. Each section limited to 10 students; instructor permission required. </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=14718">RUSS 1960 S01</a></h5>

						</div>

				</li>
										<li id="RUSS2010">
					<h4>Eighteenth-Century Literature</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">The most important literary currents from the Baroque to early romanticism. Study of style and genre and the development of the literary language. </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=15155">RUSS 2010 S01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Levitsky</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																					
																								</div>
						
				</li>
										<li id="RUSS2810">
					<h4>Russian Poetry: Silver Age</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">Exploration of the writings of such Russian poets as Blok, Tsvetaeva, Pasternak, Mandelshtam – in the context of social and cultural changes that shook Russia in first  decades of the twentieth century. The class will be conducted in English, but the poetry will be read in the original. Primary goal of the class is to teach students to analyze and discuss the complexities of poetic expression. The class is geared toward graduate students in Slavic but it is open to qualified upper level undergraduates, i.e. to those who can read  poetry assignments in original. Instructor permission required. </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=15161">RUSS 2810 S01</a></h5>

<script type="text/javascript">
	// @todo: make show/hide link dynamically generated
	$(document).ready(function(){
	
		$(".course-list .additional-sections").hide();

		// add additional sections toggle link
		$(".course-list .additional-sections").each(function(i,el){
			var numSections = $(".section", $(this)).length;
			numSections = (numSections == 1) ? numSections + " additional section" : numSections + " additional sections";
			var anchor = $(this).parents("li").attr('id');
			$(this).after('<span class="section-count">[<a href="#' + anchor + '">Show ' + numSections + '</a>]</span>');
		});

		// now add the show/hide event listeners		
		$(".section-count").each(function(i,el){
			$("a", this).bind("click keypress", function(){
				$(".additional-sections", $(this).parents("li")).slideToggle("fast");
				window.location.hash = $(this).attr("href");
				if($(this).html().match(/Show/)) {
					$(this).html($(this).html().replace("Show", "Hide"));
				} else if($(this).html().match(/Hide/)) {
					$(this).html($(this).html().replace("Hide", "Show"));
				}
				this.text(($('#toggle').text() == 'Show more') ? 'Show less' : 'Show more');
				return false;
			});
		});
		
		if (window.location.hash) {
			var hash = window.location.hash;
			if(hash.match(/#[0-9]{4}/)) {
				$(hash +  " .additional-sections").slideDown("fast");
				$(hash +  " a[href='"+hash+"']").html($(hash +  " a[href='"+hash+"']").html().replace("Show", "Hide"));
			}
		}

	});
</script>

				<section id="banner" class="marginator sub-banner">
<a href="/academics/slavic-studies/"><img src="/academics/slavic-studies/sites/brown.edu.academics.slavic-studies/files/pawtucket_simple_banner_image.jpg" /></a>
<div class="banner-text">
				<h1><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/" title="" accesskey="2"><span class="site-title"></span></a></h1><div id="site-slogan" class="slogan banner-subtext"></div>			</div></section>
		    
  <!-- Layout -->
  <div id="content">
    <div class="marginator">
                  <div class="columns main-columns">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Courses for Fall 2017</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                              <div id="tabs-wrapper" class="clear-block">
            <ul class="tabs primary">
              <li ><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/czch">CZCH</a></li>
<li ><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/plsh">PLSH</a></li>
<li ><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/russ">RUSS</a></li>
<li class="active" ><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/slav" class="active">SLAV</a></li>

            </ul>
          </div>
                                        <div class="clear-block"> <div class="content">



		<div class="course-section" id="slav">
			
				<ul class="course-list">
										<li id="SLAV1300">
					<h4>Sociolinguistics (with Case Studies on the Former USSR and Eastern Europe)</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">This seminar course examines the relationship between language and society: e.g. gender and language, politeness, terms of address, conversational analysis, dialects and language, language variation and social class, language policies and their consequences, language and national/ethnic identity. Case-study readings cover (but are not limited to) linguistic situations in East Europe, Russia, and the former republics of the USSR. Knowledge of Slavic languages not required. Open to advanced undergraduate and graduate students. Freshmen and sophomores who demonstrate their knowledge of the basic notions in linguistics or their familiarity with the former USSR and East Europe may enroll with the instructor’s written permission. Enrollment limited to 20.  DPLL WRIT </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/courses/detail?term=201710&crn=15148">SLAV 1300 S01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Fidler</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																					
																								</div>
						
				</li>

Enrollment permitted only after the written proposal (instructions in the department office) is submitted to the Concentration Advisor and Chair of the department (deadline: the last day of <i>Add a course without fee</i> period during the semester when the project is undertaken). Please check Banner for the correct section number and CRN to use when registering for this course. Each section limited to 10 students; instructor permission required. </div>

					<div class="course-overview">Independent research on various topics in Slavic cultures. Reading, discussion, research must be done in the chosen Slavic language (Czech/Russian).  Close work with faculty on project is expected. Prerequisites: minimum RUSS0600/CZCH 0610 (3rd year-level) or placement evaluation by Russian or Czech language coordinator. Enrollment permitted only after the written proposal (instructions in the department office) is submitted to the Concentration Advisor and Chair of the department (deadline: the last day of <i>Add a course without fee</i> period during the semester when the project is undertaken).  Each section limited to 10 students; instructor permission required. </div>

<script type="text/javascript">
	// @todo: make show/hide link dynamically generated
	$(document).ready(function(){
	
		$(".course-list .additional-sections").hide();

		// add additional sections toggle link
		$(".course-list .additional-sections").each(function(i,el){
			var numSections = $(".section", $(this)).length;
			numSections = (numSections == 1) ? numSections + " additional section" : numSections + " additional sections";
			var anchor = $(this).parents("li").attr('id');
			$(this).after('<span class="section-count">[<a href="#' + anchor + '">Show ' + numSections + '</a>]</span>');
		});

		// now add the show/hide event listeners		
		$(".section-count").each(function(i,el){
			$("a", this).bind("click keypress", function(){
				$(".additional-sections", $(this).parents("li")).slideToggle("fast");
				window.location.hash = $(this).attr("href");
				if($(this).html().match(/Show/)) {
					$(this).html($(this).html().replace("Show", "Hide"));
				} else if($(this).html().match(/Hide/)) {
					$(this).html($(this).html().replace("Hide", "Show"));
				}
				this.text(($('#toggle').text() == 'Show more') ? 'Show less' : 'Show more');
				return false;
			});
		});
		
		if (window.location.hash) {
			var hash = window.location.hash;
			if(hash.match(/#[0-9]{4}/)) {
				$(hash +  " .additional-sections").slideDown("fast");
				$(hash +  " a[href='"+hash+"']").html($(hash +  " a[href='"+hash+"']").html().replace("Show", "Hide"));
			}
		}

	});
</script>

				<h1><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/" title="" accesskey="2"><span class="site-title"></span></a></h1><div id="site-slogan" class="slogan banner-subtext"></div>			</div></section>

        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Graduate</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
<article id="node-13" class="main-article node">








  <div class="content">
        <h2>Graduate Student Curriculum</h2>
<h2>The Ph.D. Degree</h2>
<p>The Department of Slavic Studies offers a comprehensive doctoral program in Slavic studies specializing in Russian literature and culture, in modern Czech culture, and in Polish literature and culture.</p>
<p>The program has a strong interdisciplinary focus and students are expected to work with departmental faculty as well as with faculty in related fields, such as comparative literature, theater, history, art history, modern culture and media, and political science. The program will train flexible and innovative scholars able to address varying teaching and research needs in the future job market. We particularly target advanced students who would come to Brown with a strong background in at least one of the program's key disciplines (literature, language, culture, theater, social sciences). Students receive close guidance and are mentored in the pedagogy of language and literature/culture teaching.</p>
<p><strong>Completion Requirements</strong><br /> <strong>A.M.</strong>: Eight courses, approved by the department</p>
<p><strong>Ph.D.</strong>: Sixteen courses, including five graduate seminars, and two to four courses in a secondary field of study; theory and methods of foreign language teaching, reading knowledge of the second language related to the student's specialization; teaching; qualifying examinations; dissertation and defense.</p>
<p><strong>Admission Information</strong><br /> <strong>Admission Requirements</strong>: Advanced competence in Russian. Writing sample in English (12-15 pages). Knowledge/interest in another Slavic language (preferably Czech or Polish) in encouraged but not required.</p>
<p><strong>GRE General</strong>: Required<br /> <strong>GRE Subject</strong>: Not required<br /> <strong>Application Deadline</strong>: January 7</p>
<p>For more information, please contact&nbsp;<a href="mailto:vladimir_golstein@brown.edu " rel="nofollow">vladimir_golstein@brown.edu</a> or&nbsp;<a href="mailto:alexander_levitsky@brown.edu" rel="nofollow">alexander_levitsky@brown.edu</a>, Directors of Graduate Study.</p>
<h2>The Master of Arts Degree</h2>
<p>The Master's degree is often sought as a terminal degree by  students planning careers in fields where advanced work is useful but a  doctorate is not required. Work for this degree may be in Russian  language and literature or in Slavic linguistics. The Master's program  normally consists of eight semester courses approved by the Department. A  spoken and written command of Russian is required of candidates for  this degree as well as a reading knowledge of another Slavic language or  French or German. A thesis is not required. A student enrolled in  full-time study can expect to complete all requirements for the master's  degree within one academic year. Information about the application can  be found at the<a href="http://www.brown.edu/gradschool/apply/online-application"> Brown Graduate School Admissions website</a>.</p>
<p>For more information, please contact <a href="mailto:vladimir_golstein@brown.edu">vladimir_golstein@brown.edu</a> or <a href="mailto:alexander_levitsky@brown.edu">alexander_levitsky@brown.edu</a>, Directors of Graduate Study.</p>
  </div>

<div class="banner-text">
				<h1><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/" title="" accesskey="2"><span class="site-title"></span></a></h1><div id="site-slogan" class="slogan banner-subtext"></div>			</div></section>

                  <div class="columns main-columns">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Courses</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
<article id="node-168" class="main-article node">








  <div class="content">
        <h5><strong>Graduate Student Courses and Teaching<br /></strong></h5>
<p><strong></strong>The Department offers all levels of instruction in Russian language, literature, and culture. Upper level <a href="http://brown.edu/academics/slavic-studies/undergraduate/courses#RUSS">Russian language courses</a>, in addition to all advanced literature and culture courses (sequences above 1000), serve both graduate students and undergraduate concentrators in Slavic Studies; they also attract students whose interests range across the entire university curriculum.</p>
<p>Students of International Relations and Comparative Literature are particularly well-represented among our learners, quite a few of whom go on to study and/or work abroad. All students in need of advanced levels of instruction in Russian make considerable use of the state-of-the-art audio-visual and multimedia offerings of <a href="http://www.brown.edu/Departments/LRC/">Brown's Language Resource Center</a>. Our language courses also provide valuable classroom experience to graduate students in the Department preparing for teaching careers.</p>
<p>An appointment as a <a href="http://brown.edu/academics/slavic-studies/graduate/teaching">Teaching Assistant or Teaching Fellow</a> requires taking part both in a pre-service Second Language TA Workshop and in-service meetings with the course coordinator. These acquaint TAs with issues of language acquisition and pedagogy, and seek to influence both the development of the TAs' philosophy of teaching and their teaching practice.</p>
<h5>Suggested Courses</h5>
<p style="padding-left:30px">Eighteenth-Century Russian Literature (RUSS2010)<br />Movements and Genres in Russian Literary Culture (RUSS2410)<br />Seminars in Russian Literature (RUSS2610, 2620, 2710, 2720)<br />Theories of Literature (COLT2650)<br />Seminar in the History of Early Modern Europe (HI2070)<br />Seminar in European Social History in the Eighteenth and Nineteenth Centuries (HIST 2080)<br />Revolution as a Work of Art (TAPS2120)<br />Abstraction and Resistance (TAPS2200)<br />Proseminar in Political Theory (POLS2120)<br />Theory and Methods of Foreign Language Teaching (GRMN, FREN2900)</p>
<p>More detailed course information can be found by performing a search on <a href="http://courses.brown.edu/">Brown's Course Preview</a>. For best results, search under the RUSS, CZCH, PLSH, and SLAV rubrics, as well as COLT, TAPS, HIST, POLS, and INTL.</p>
  </div>

  <div class="content">
        <p><strong>Piotr Axer</strong><br /><a href="mailto:piotr_axer@brown.edu" rel="nofollow">piotr_axer@brown.edu</a></p>

<a href="/academics/slavic-studies/"><img src="/academics/slavic-studies/sites/brown.edu.academics.slavic-studies/files/pawtucket_simple_banner_image.jpg" /></a>
<div class="banner-text">
				<h1><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/" title="" accesskey="2"><span class="site-title"></span></a></h1><div id="site-slogan" class="slogan banner-subtext"></div>			</div></section>
		    
  <!-- Layout -->
  <div id="content">
    <div class="marginator">
                  <div class="columns main-columns">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">PhD Requirements</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
<article id="node-402" class="main-article node">








  <div class="content">
        <h2>The Ph.D. Degree</h2>
<p>The doctoral program in Slavic Studies focuses largely on modern  Russian and Czech cultures. The doctoral program in these regions  thereby covers a critical area of European and Eurasian studies at  Brown. The program's vigor derives from strong and dedicated faculty,  including 7 full time Slavic Department faculty and 3 faculty with joint  appointments in Slavic and related departments.</p>
<p>The doctoral program in Slavic Studies distinguishes itself  from traditional programs in Slavic that focus exclusively on literary  studies. It allows for variable degrees of interdisciplinary and  intercultural studies. Students work with departmental faculty as well  as with faculty in related fields such as comparative literature,  theater and performance studies, history, political science, and  international relations. Students in our program are prepared to become  flexible and innovative scholars in their research and teaching, who  address varying teaching and research needs in the future job market.  Outstanding library holdings in West and South Slavic languages and  cultures at Brown and courses through Brown-Harvard exchange program  offer yet additional excellent resources for research.</p>
<p>In addition to receiving training in related disciplines, the  doctoral students amass experience in teaching languages and  literatures. Mentoring in teaching occurs in various contexts: in  language and literature courses, where they serve as teaching  assistants, in the interdepartmental foreign language teaching methods  course (and related practice), and in seminars at <a href="http://www.brown.edu/Administration/Sheridan_Center/">The Sheridan Center for Teaching and Learning</a>. Students will receive extensive advice on research strategies, conference presentations, and publication of their works. Additional information is available at the <a href="https://www.brown.edu/academics/gradschool/programs/slavic-studies">Graduate School Program website</a>.</p>
<h2>Requirements</h2>
<ol>
<li>16 graduate-level courses, including:
<ul>
<li>A minimum of five 200-level graduate seminars</li>
<li>Theory and Methods of Foreign Language Teaching</li>
<li>Two to four courses in a related field (to be determined in consultation with the Director of Graduate Study)</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="http://brown.edu/academics/slavic-studies/graduate/teaching">Teaching</a> (minimum 3 semesters).&nbsp; An effort will be made to  provide teaching experience not only in a Slavic language, but also in  Russian literature, culture, and history.</li>
<li>Reading knowledge of the second language closely related  to the student's specialization. A standard of professional competence  should be maintained within the area of likely specialization. Most  students intending to specialize in Slavic cultural studies should  demonstrate an appropriate language competence in Russian and one more  Slavic language, normally Czech, and most students specializing in one  Slavic culture need German or French for their research. This  requirement may be satisfied through advanced course during the first  year, or by placement evaluation. Fulfillment of the second language  requirement with a language other than German or French must be approved  by the graduate committee.</li>
<li>Qualifying Examination (information available in <a href="http://brown.edu/academics/slavic-studies/about/contact">the department office</a>)</li>
<li>Dissertation and Defense (information available in the department  office). Students should submit the doctoral thesis prospectus to the  thesis director and the Director of Graduate Study by October 1 of their  fourth year.</li>
<li>Students whose primary Slavic language competence  requires them to take language courses below the 100 level may do so in  consultation with the Director of Graduate Study, but those courses will  not count toward the course requirements for the Ph.D.</li>
</ol>
<h2>Funding and Time Table for Completion of the Ph.D. in Slavic Studies</h2>
<p>Normally course work and the preliminary examinations are  completed by the end of the third year, submission of the doctoral  thesis proposal during the fourth, and one or two years of work to  complete the doctoral thesis. We expect our students to be supported by  scholarships during their first year, by<a href="../../Departments/Slavic_Languages/grad/teachingassistant.html" rel="nofollow"> </a><a href="http://brown.edu/academics/slavic-studies/graduate/teaching">teaching fellowships/assistantships</a><a href="../../Departments/Slavic_Languages/grad/teachingassistant.html" rel="nofollow"> </a>during their second to fourth years, and by a dissertation fellowship during their last year.</p>
  </div>

	
  <div class="clear-block">
    <div class="meta">


	    
		</div><!-- end .meta -->
	</div>

</article>

<div class="banner-text">
				<h1><a href="/academics/slavic-studies/" title="" accesskey="2"><span class="site-title"></span></a></h1><div id="site-slogan" class="slogan banner-subtext"></div>			</div></section>
		    
  <!-- Layout -->
  <div id="content">
    <div class="marginator">
                  <div class="columns main-columns">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Svejkauskas Award</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
<article id="node-170" class="main-article node">








  <div class="content">
        <p><strong>The Dr. Pranas A. Sveikauskas Award</strong> is given to graduating Ph.Ds who have written outstanding dissertations. Past recipients include:</p>
<p>2006&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Sofya Khagi<br />2005&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Natalia Lechtchenko<br />2005&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Kerry Ann Sabbag<br />2004&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Marina Aptekman<br />2004&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Charles Henry Arndt III<br />2004&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Heather Mae Daly<br />2004&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Olga Simonova Partan<br />2000&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; David Lindgren Gehrenbeck<br />1998&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Maria Rubins<br />1997&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Natalie Foshko<br />1997&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Alisa Gayle Mayor<br />1997&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Laura Souders<br />1997&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Arkady Yanishevsky<br />1996&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Olga B. Strakhov<br />1994&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Thomas Ralph Epstein<br />1993&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Lawrence Kevin Mansour<br />1993&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Thomas Hilary Oller<br />1992&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Maurice LaBauve Hebert<br />1992&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Claudia Novack-Jones<br />1990&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Laura Jo Turner McCullough</p>
  </div>

	</div>

        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Undergraduate Program</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
<article id="node-12" class="main-article node">








  <div class="content">
        <h2>Undergraduate Program in the Department of Slavic Studies</h2>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p>What is Slavic? The term<span> refers to the branch of the Indo-European language family that includes Russian, Ukrainian, and Belorussian (<span>East Slavic</span>), Polish, Czech, Sorbian, Slovak (<span>West Slavic</span>), and Bulgarian, Slovenian, Bosnian/Croatian/Serbian<em>, </em>and Macedonian<em> </em>(<span>South Slavic</span>). The number of speakers of all Slavic languages is estimated to be 315 million, of which the most commonly spoken languages are Russian (145 million), Polish (43 million), Ukrainian (39.5 million), Czech (11 million), and Serbian (11 million). In addition, Russian is used as a second language in most of the countries of the former Soviet Union.</span></p>
<p><span>The Department of Slavic Studies at Brown focuses on three of the most commonly spoken Slavic languages: Russian, Czech, and Polish. Although closely related linguistically and geographically, Russia, Poland, and the Czech Republic followed different paths in history, culture, religion, arts, and politics. Yet their histories are interrelated and exemplify both cultural cross-fertilization and often tumultuous confrontations that are connected with national aspirations and ambitions. They continue to be key players in the constantly changing political landscape of Central and Eastern Europe; their recent histories—most notably Poland and the Czech Republic &nbsp;joining of the European Union—reflect the tensions and hopes of all European countries.</span></p>
<p><span>Our program’s objective is to provide students who are interested in Russian, Polish, and Czech languages, literatures, histories and cultures with an in-depth understanding of cultural, economic, and political processes in Eastern and Central Europe. Since the collapse of the Soviet Union and the East European Socialist bloc, these countries have undergone rapid economic and political changes and actively engaged in global politics. The professional paths of our former concentrators demonstrate that studying Russian and/or Polish and Czech is a major asset to students considering careers in such diverse fields as international relations and diplomacy, law, business, teaching and academic research. Our program allows students to engage deeply with some of the richest literary traditions in the world, and to examine them in their historical, political contexts – from Russian classics like the works of Dostoevsky, Tolstoy, Chekhov and Nabokov, to brilliant Central and East European writers like Schulz, Gombrowicz, Hrabal and Kundera.&nbsp;</span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</p>
  </div>
